<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><i><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a></i></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="5/5 stars"><img alt="5/5 stars" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" title="5/5 stars" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[205]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In his 1969 <i><a href="/wiki/Pop_Chronicles" title="Pop Chronicles">Pop Chronicles</a></i> series, <a href="/wiki/John_Gilliland" title="John Gilliland">John Gilliland</a> stated that the album was almost overshadowed by the Beatles' <i><a href="/wiki/Revolver_(Beatles_album)" title="Revolver (Beatles album)">Revolver</a></i>, released two months later, and that "a lot people failed to realize that Brian Wilson's production was as unique in its own way as the Beatles'".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc37_59-4"><a href="#cite_note-pc37-59">[49]</a></sup> Writing in the first edition of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stone_Record_Guide" title="The Rolling Stone Record Guide">The Rolling Stone Record Guide</a></i> (1979), <a href="/wiki/Dave_Marsh" title="Dave Marsh">Dave Marsh</a> gave <i>Pet Sounds</i> four stars (out of a possible five) and described it as a "powerful, but spotty" collection on which the least experimental songs proved to be the best.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshSwenson198330_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshSwenson198330-237">[206]</a></sup> Five years later, he wrote that the album was now considered a "classic", elaborating: "<i>Pet Sounds</i> wasn't a commercial flop, but it did signal that the group was losing contact with its listeners (a charge that could not be leveled against the Beatles during the same period)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1985114_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1985114-238">[207]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i> theorized that the later success of "Good Vibrations" was what helped turn around the perception of <i>Pet Sounds</i>; that the "un-hip orchestrations and pervasive sadness baffled some longtime fans, who didn't immediately get what Wilson was trying to do."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AVPrimer_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-AVPrimer-239">[208]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 89%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>By God if this little record didn't change only the course of popular music, but the course of a few lives in the bargain ... nobody was prepared for anything so soulful, so lovely, something one had to think about so much.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">—<a href="/wiki/Stephen_Davis_(music_journalist)" title="Stephen Davis (music journalist)">Stephen Davis</a> in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)" title="Rolling Stone (magazine)">Rolling Stone</a></i>, June 1972<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis1972_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davis1972-240">[209]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Davis_(music_journalist)" title="Stephen Davis (music journalist)">Stephen Davis</a>'s 1972 <i>Rolling Stone</i> review, Davis called <i>Pet Sounds</i> "by far" Brian Wilson's best album and said that its "trenchant cycle of love songs has the emotional impact of a shatteringly evocative novel".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis1972_240-1"><a href="#cite_note-Davis1972-240">[209]</a></sup> In <i>Music USA: The Rough Guide</i>, Richie Unterberger and Samb Hicks deemed the album to be a "quantum leap" from the Beach Boys' earlier material, and "the most gorgeous arrangements ever to grace a rock record".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnterbergerHicks1999382_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnterbergerHicks1999382-241">[210]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_New_York_Observer" title="The New York Observer">The New York Observer</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s D. Strauss says that the album's quality and subversion of rock traditions is "what created its special place in rock history; there was no category for its fans to place it in".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strauss1997_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Strauss1997-242">[211]</a></sup> in Author Luis Sanchez views the album as "the score to a film about what rock music doesn't have to be. For all of its inward-looking sentimentalism, it lays out in a masterful way the kind of glow and <i>sui generis</i> vision that Brian aimed to [later] expand."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESanchez201483_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESanchez201483-186">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Dominique_Leone" title="Dominique Leone">Dominique Leone</a> wrote a 9.4 review of its <i>40th Anniversary</i> edition for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a> stating: "Certainly, regardless of what I write here, the impact and 'influence' of the record will have been in turn hardly influenced at all. I can't even get my dad to talk about <i>Pet Sounds</i> anymore. ... The hymnal aspect of many of these songs seems no less pronounced, and the general air of deeply heartfelt love, graciousness and the uncertainty that any of it will be returned are still affecting to the point of distraction."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pitchfork2006_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork2006-122">[105]</a></sup> Music journalist <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> felt that <i>Pet Sounds</i> was a good record, but believed it had become looked upon as a <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/totem#noun" title="wikt:totem">totem</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[212]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the 1990s, three British critics' polls would feature <i>Pet Sounds</i> at or near the top of their lists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoeTobler200919_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoeTobler200919-90">[74]</a></sup> Those who have deemed it "the greatest album of all time" include <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NME1_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-NME1-244">[213]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheTimes1_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheTimes1-245">[214]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Uncut_(magazine)" title="Uncut (magazine)">Uncut</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UncutGreatest2016_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-UncutGreatest2016-246">[215]</a></sup> In 1998, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Recording_Arts_and_Sciences" title="National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences">National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences</a> inducted the album into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Hall_of_Fame_Award" title="Grammy Hall of Fame Award">Grammy Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[216]</a></sup> In 2004, <i>Pet Sounds</i> was preserved in the <a href="/wiki/National_Recording_Registry" title="National Recording Registry">National Recording Registry</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a> for being "culturally, historically, or aesthetically significant."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Congress_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Congress-4">[4]</a></sup> As of 2006, more than 100 domestic and international publications and journalists have lauded <i>Pet Sounds</i> as one of the greatest albums ever recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMIssions_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-EMIssions-248">[217]</a></sup> In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Acclaimed_Music" title="Acclaimed Music">Acclaimed Music</a>, which statistically aggregates hundreds of published lists, ranked <i>Pet Sounds</i> as the most acclaimed album of all-time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RacismPM_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-RacismPM-6">[6]</a></sup> After being asked where somebody should begin with the Beach Boys discography, Wilson said, "They should listen to <i>Pet Sounds</i> first, and then listen to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys_Love_You" title="The Beach Boys Love You">The Beach Boys Love You</a></i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[218]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_and_legacy">Influence and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Influence and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cultural_impact_of_the_Beach_Boys" title="Cultural impact of the Beach Boys">Cultural impact of the Beach Boys</a></div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 89%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>It's been said that, although hardly anyone bought <a href="/wiki/The_Velvet_Underground" title="The Velvet Underground">the Velvet Underground</a>'s records, those who did ended up being inspired to start their own bands. In the case of the Beach Boys' 1966 opus <i>Pet Sounds</i>, it's likely that each of its 13 songs inspired its own subset of pop offspring,</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">—Jeff Straton, <i><a href="/wiki/New_Times_Broward-Palm_Beach" title="New Times Broward-Palm Beach">New Times Broward-Palm Beach</a></i>, October 2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[219]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>In 2009, author Chris Smith commented that "<i>Pet Sounds</i> still stands as one of the most innovative recordings in rock and elevated Brian Wilson from talented bandleader to studio genius".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200938_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200938-119">[102]</a></sup> Although not originally a big seller, <i>Pet Sounds</i> has been enormously influential since it was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200938_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200938-119">[102]</a></sup> Writer Rachael Maddux discussed the album's impact in 2011: "These days, the legacy of <i>Pet Sounds</i> looms so large that you can't always be sure if what you're hearing takes a direct line from the album itself or if it pulls from a second tier one of the hundreds of thousands of its beneficiaries now trickling down their own influence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SixDegrees_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-SixDegrees-94">[78]</a></sup> In 1995, a panel of numerous musicians, songwriters and producers assembled by <i>MOJO</i> voted <i>Pet Sounds</i> as the greatest album among them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[220]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Pet Sounds</i> is credited for advancing the field of music production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoorefield201016_160-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoorefield201016-160">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin199839.E2.80.9342_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin199839.E2.80.9342-252">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones200854_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones200854-253">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZager2012181_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZager2012181-254">[223]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="How exactly do these sources characterize the album's advances? (December 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1971, publication <i>Beat Instrumental &amp; International Recording</i> wrote: "<i>Pet Sounds</i> took everyone by surprise. In terms of musical conception, lyric content, production and performance, it stood as a landmark in a music genre whose development was about to begin snowballing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[224]</a></sup> The same year, <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">Cue</a></i> magazine reflected that "in the year and a half that followed <i>Pet Sounds</i>, the Beach Boys were among the vanguard in practically every aspect of the <a href="/wiki/Counterculture" title="Counterculture">counter culture</a> ... anticipating changes that rock didn't accomplish until 1969–1970."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[225]</a></sup> The album's historical distinctions include being the first piece in popular music to incorporate the Electro-Theremin, an easier-to-play version of the <a href="/wiki/Theremin" title="Theremin">theremin</a>, as well as the first in rock music to feature a theremin-like instrument.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambert2007240_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambert2007240-257">[226]</a></sup> The Electro-Theremin's inventor <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tanner" title="Paul Tanner">Paul Tanner</a> performs the instrument on the song "I Just Wasn't Made for These Times".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tracks_36-10"><a href="#cite_note-tracks-36">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoeTobler200926_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoeTobler200926-258">[227]</a></sup></p>
<p>The album informed the developments of genres such as rock, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hip-hop" title="Hip-hop">hip-hop</a>, jazz, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic</a>, experimental, <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a>, pop,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pitchfork50_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork50-259">[228]</a></sup> and is often cited as one of the earliest entries in the canon of psychedelic rock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SixDegrees_94-2"><a href="#cite_note-SixDegrees-94">[78]</a></sup> Scholar Philip Auslander explains that even though psychedelic music is not normally associated with the Beach Boys, the "odd directions" and experiments in <i>Pet Sounds</i> "put it all on the map. ... basically that sort of opened the door — not for groups to be formed or to start to make music, but certainly to become as visible as say <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Airplane" title="Jefferson Airplane">Jefferson Airplane</a> or somebody like that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Longman2016_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-Longman2016-260">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[nb 32]</a></sup> Many Los Angeles record producers imitated the album's orchestral style, which became a component to the <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_pop" title="Sunshine pop">sunshine pop</a> acts that followed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[230]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Reader" title="Chicago Reader">Chicago Reader</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> <a href="/wiki/Noah_Berlatsky" title="Noah Berlatsky">Noah Berlatsky</a> argued that the Beach Boys helped develop <a href="/wiki/Smooth_soul" title="Smooth soul">smooth soul</a>, bridging a gap between the polished pop harmonizing of <a href="/wiki/The_Drifters" title="The Drifters">the Drifters</a> and the experimentation of <a href="/wiki/The_Chi-Lites" title="The Chi-Lites">the Chi-Lites</a>, particularly with "Sloop John B", whose "fussy" arrangements, "pure" harmonies, and "childish vulnerability" he says "come out of a tradition of pop R&amp;B".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[231]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Pet Sounds</i> predicated progressive pop<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[232]</a></sup> and part of <a href="/wiki/Chamber_pop" title="Chamber pop">chamber pop</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CollinsInc_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-CollinsInc-265">[233]</a></sup> <i>Treblezine</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Ernest Simpson and <a href="/wiki/Wild_Nothing" title="Wild Nothing">Wild Nothing</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jack_Tatum" title="Jack Tatum">Jack Tatum</a> characterize it as the first <a href="/wiki/Emo" title="Emo">emo</a> album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pitchfork50_259-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork50-259">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[nb 33]</a></sup> Composer/journalist <a href="/wiki/Frank_J._Oteri" title="Frank J. Oteri">Frank Oteri</a> called it a "clear precedent" to the birth of <a href="/wiki/Album-oriented_rock" title="Album-oriented rock">album-oriented rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oteri2011_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oteri2011-269">[236]</a></sup> Author <a href="/wiki/Bill_Martin_(philosophy)" title="Bill Martin (philosophy)">Bill Martin</a> felt that the album represented a turning point for progressive rock as the Beach Boys and the Beatles transformed rock music from <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance music</a> into music that was made for listening to, bringing "expansions in <a href="/wiki/Harmony" title="Harmony">harmony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arrangement" title="Arrangement">instrumentation</a> (and therefore <a href="/wiki/Timbre" title="Timbre">timbre</a>), <a href="/wiki/Duration_(music)" title="Duration (music)">duration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhythm" title="Rhythm">rhythm</a>, and the use of <a href="/wiki/History_of_multitrack_recording" title="History of multitrack recording">recording technology</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin199839.E2.80.9342_252-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin199839.E2.80.9342-252">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[nb 34]</a></sup> It is viewed by David Leaf as a herald of the <a href="/wiki/Art_rock" title="Art rock">art rock</a> genre,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeaf198574_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeaf198574-103">[87]</a></sup> while Jones specifically locates it to the genre's beginning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones200849_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones200849-102">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[nb 35]</a></sup> Its innovations would echo in the art rock of the 1970s and the <a href="/wiki/Indie_pop" title="Indie pop">indie pop</a> of the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[240]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abandoning_formula">Abandoning formula</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Abandoning formula">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Progressive_music" title="Progressive music">Progressive music</a></div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 89%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>While many may struggle to see the direct link between the bright, bouncy tones of <i>Pet Sounds</i> and bands like the Beatles, <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a> and countless prog-rock bands, there was simply no precedent for the way that notes moved and vibrated across the record.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">—Joel Freimark, January 2016<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[241]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Perone's assessment of the album's composition indicates a remove from "just about anything else that was going on in 1966 pop music".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerone201228_128-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerone201228-128">[111]</a></sup> Composer <a href="/wiki/Philip_Glass" title="Philip Glass">Philip Glass</a> observed: "Listening to it today, it is, perhaps, easier to see why it was one of the defining moments of its time ... its willingness to abandon formula in favor of structural innovation, the introduction of classical elements in the arrangements, production concepts in terms of overall sound which were novel at the time-all these elements give <i>Pet Sounds</i> a freshness that, 30 years later, is immediately there for the listener."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[242]</a></sup> Strauss writes that with <i>Pet Sounds</i>, the Beach Boys became the first major rock group "to look music trends firmly in the eye and declare that rock really didn’t matter. Rock is supposed to be about, you know, fucking, and Brian Wilson was recording a song ('I Know There’s an Answer') that was originally entitled 'Get Rid of Your Libido'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strauss1997_242-1"><a href="#cite_note-Strauss1997-242">[211]</a></sup> Sommer said that the Beach Boys became the first group to make an entire album that departed from the usual small-ensemble electric rock band format: "Of course, others had done it for a song or two, but no one had said, 'This will be a complete album that can not be performed by four or five guys plugged into amps. ... Once the Beach Boys let that cat out of the bag, the whole ship of rock sailed to new ports.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sommer2016_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sommer2016-113">[97]</a></sup> Comparing <i>Pet Sounds</i> to other albums that are often labeled "masterpieces", such as <i><a href="/wiki/OK_Computer" title="OK Computer">OK Computer</a></i> (1997), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dark_Side_of_the_Moon" title="Dark Side of the Moon">Dark Side of the Moon</a></i> (1973) or <i><a href="/wiki/Thick_as_a_Brick" title="Thick as a Brick">Thick as a Brick</a></i> (1972), Sommer notes "only <i>Pet Sounds</i> is written from the teen or adolescent point of view."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sommer2016_113-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sommer2016-113">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Professor of American history <a href="/wiki/John_Robert_Greene" title="John Robert Greene">John Robert Greene</a> stated that "God Only Knows" remade the ideal of the popular love song, while "Sloop John B" and "Pet Sounds" broke new ground and took rock music away from its casual lyrics and melodic structures into what was then uncharted territory. He furthermore called it one factor which spawned the majority of trends in post-1965 rock music, the only others being the Beatles' <i>Rubber Soul</i> (1965) and <i>Revolver</i> (1966), and the 1960s folk movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreene2010155_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreene2010155-278">[243]</a></sup> Similar to subsequent experimental rock LPs by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Zappa" title="Frank Zappa">Frank Zappa</a>, the Beatles, and the Who, <i>Pet Sounds</i> featured countertextural aspects that called attention to the very recordedness of the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELowe200738.2C_219_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELowe200738.2C_219-279">[244]</a></sup> Many British groups responded to the album by making more experimental use of recording studio techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGillett1984329_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGillett1984329-215">[184]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gang_of_Four_(band)" title="Gang of Four (band)">Gang of Four's</a> Andy Gill posited: "<i>Pet Sounds</i> is not a knowing record. It’s innocent, but so many rock bands took it as a green light to get clever — to start playing with the time signatures, to go prog. You know, "Let’s put a french horn in there!" Before you know it, you’ve got Queen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CoSJune2016_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-CoSJune2016-280">[245]</a></sup></p>
<p>Released on the same day as <i>Pet Sounds</i> was <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Blonde_on_Blonde" title="Blonde on Blonde">Blonde on Blonde</a></i>, which Leibovitz calls "two strands in the same conversation, the one that turned American popular music, for one fleeting moment of one year in the middle 1960s, into a religious movement".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lebo2016_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lebo2016-136">[119]</a></sup> Author Geoffrey Himes explains: "The challenge for the pop songwriter is to mirror real life's conflicts in the song and still deliver the satisfying resolution pop music requires. Bob Dylan did it by introducing irony into rock'n'roll lyrics, and Brian's introduction of non-standard harmonies and timbres proved just as revolutionary ... Most pop music unifies its lyric, melodic, harmonic and rhythmic devices so it can communicate one simple emotion as powerfully as possible. ... This unified approach can be quite satisfying, but it can't reflect the complications of adult emotions in real life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HimesSurf_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-HimesSurf-56">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rock_as_art">Rock as art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Rock as art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_rock" title="Art rock">Art rock</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Album_Era" title="Album Era">Album Era</a></div>
<p><i>The New York Observer</i> wrote that "<i>Pet Sounds</i> proved that a pop group could make an album-length piece comparable with the greatest long-form works of <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Bernstein" title="Leonard Bernstein">Bernstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Copland" title="Aaron Copland">Copland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ives" title="Charles Ives">Ives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rodgers_and_Hammerstein" title="Rodgers and Hammerstein">Rodgers and Hammerstein</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sommer2015_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sommer2015-112">[96]</a></sup> According to music journalists Stephen Davis and Nick Kent, <i>Pet Sounds</i> was the first rock concept album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKent200923.E2.80.9324_141-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKent200923.E2.80.9324-141">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis1972_240-2"><a href="#cite_note-Davis1972-240">[209]</a></sup> Bill Holdship said that it was "perhaps rock's first example of self-conscious art".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holdship_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holdship-281">[246]</a></sup> According to Jim Fusilli, author of the <a href="/wiki/33%E2%85%93" title="33⅓">33⅓</a> book on the album, it "[raised itself] to the level of art through its musical sophistication and the precision of its statement",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFusilli2005116.E2.80.93119_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFusilli2005116.E2.80.93119-282">[247]</a></sup> while academic Michael Johnson said that the album was one of the first documented moments of ascension in rock music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnson2009197_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnson2009197-283">[248]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">The Atlantic</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Jason Guriel credited <i>Pet Sounds</i> with inventing "the modern pop album", that Wilson "certainly anticipated the modern pop-centric era, which privileges producer over artist and blurs the line between entertainment and art. ... Wilson patented a type that lives on to this day— that of the reclusive genius whose instrument is the entire studio. <i>Pet Sounds</i> foreshadowed the big-budget psychodramas of the future—albums by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radiohead" title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>, and other skittish artists successful enough to find a fully-stocked studio at their ego's disposal. Anytime a band or musician disappears into a studio to contrive an album-length mystery, the ghost of Wilson is hovering near."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guriel2016_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guriel2016-52">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_artists">Other artists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other artists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>focuses too much on specific examples</b> without clearly discussing its abstract general subject. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help by consulting <a href="/wiki/Secondary_source" title="Secondary source">secondary sources</a> for <b>general statements</b> made about the subject and <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by adding more <b>general information</b>.</span> <small><i>(February 2016)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Among the musicians contributing to the 1966 <i>Melody Maker</i> survey, <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Davis" title="Spencer Davis">Spencer Davis</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Spencer_Davis_Group" title="The Spencer Davis Group">the Spencer Davis Group</a> said: "Brian Wilson is a great record producer. I haven't spent much time listening to the Beach Boys before, but I'm a fan now and I just want to listen to this LP again and again."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2004139_225-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2004139-225">[194]</a></sup> Then a member of <a href="/wiki/Cream_(band)" title="Cream (band)">Cream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a> reported that everyone in his band loved the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2004139_225-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2004139-225">[194]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Manfred_Mann" title="Manfred Mann">Manfred Mann</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_D%27Abo" title="Michael D'Abo">Michael D'Abo</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Walker_Brothers" title="The Walker Brothers">the Walker Brothers</a>' <a href="/wiki/Scott_Walker_(singer)" title="Scott Walker (singer)">Scott Walker</a> did not agree that the album was revolutionary or better than the Beach Boys' earlier work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MelodyMakerProgPop_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-MelodyMakerProgPop-284">[249]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a> of the <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">Who</a> opined that "the Beach Boys new material is too remote and way out. It's written for a feminine audience."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2004139_225-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2004139-225">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[nb 36]</a></sup> Journalist and television presenter <a href="/wiki/Barry_Fantoni" title="Barry Fantoni">Barry Fantoni</a> similarly preferred the group's <i>Beach Boys Today!</i> and stated that <i>Pet Sounds</i> "[is] probably revolutionary, but I'm not sure that everything that's revolutionary is necessarily good".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2004139_225-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2004139-225">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>Speaking to <i>Rolling Stone</i> in 2003, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a> said that <i>Pet Sounds</i> changed everything about records for him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[251]</a></sup> "God Only Knows" inspired songwriter <a href="/wiki/Margo_Guryan" title="Margo Guryan">Margo Guryan</a> to re-evaluate her career: "I thought it was just gorgeous. I bought the record and played it a million times, then sat down and wrote 'Think of Rain.' That's really how I started writing that way. I just decided it was better than what was happening in jazz."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[252]</a></sup> Seattle-based folk band the <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Foxes" title="Fleet Foxes">Fleet Foxes</a> have often paid tribute to the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[253]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jim_Reid" title="Jim Reid">Jim Reid</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Jesus_and_Mary_Chain" title="The Jesus and Mary Chain">the Jesus and Mary Chain</a> said it's "so obviously brilliant that it's almost beyond even talking about".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[254]</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Terence_Trent_D%27Arby" title="Terence Trent D'Arby">Terence Trent D'Arby</a> heard the album for the first time, he proceeded to play it at least once a day for the next six months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[255]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paul McCartney has frequently spoken of his affinity with the album, citing "God Only Knows" as his favorite song of all time, and crediting his melodic bass-playing style to the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCartney1997_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCartney1997-292">[256]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin1997_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martin1997-293">[257]</a></sup> He acknowledged that <i>Pet Sounds</i> was the primary impetus for the Beatles' 1967 album <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i>. The interplay between the Beatles and the Beach Boys thus inextricably links the two albums together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones200857_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones200857-294">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[nb 37]</a></sup> Arranger <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kirby" title="Robert Kirby">Robert Kirby</a> claims that English singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Nick_Drake" title="Nick Drake">Nick Drake</a> intended the instrumentals on his 1970 album <i><a href="/wiki/Bryter_Layter" title="Bryter Layter">Bryter Layter</a></i> to evoke <i>Pet Sounds</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[260]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Primal_Scream" title="Primal Scream">Primal Scream</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/Screamadelica" title="Screamadelica">Screamadelica</a></i> (1991) was influenced by <i>Pet Sounds</i>, and the band's <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Gillespie" title="Bobby Gillespie">Bobby Gillespie</a> says that after discovering the album, their songs became much softer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pitchfork50_259-2"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork50-259">[228]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/R.E.M." title="R.E.M.">R.E.M.</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/At_My_Most_Beautiful" title="At My Most Beautiful">At My Most Beautiful</a>" was written as a "gift" from <a href="/wiki/Michael_Stipe" title="Michael Stipe">Michael Stipe</a> to his bandmates, to indulge their fondness of <i>Pet Sounds</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[261]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Radiohead" title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Thom_Yorke" title="Thom Yorke">Thom Yorke</a> said that their 1997 album <i><a href="/wiki/OK_Computer" title="OK Computer">OK Computer</a></i> was influenced by the atmosphere of <i>Pet Sounds</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAUNCH_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-LAUNCH-299">[262]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Weezer" title="Weezer">Weezer</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Rivers_Cuomo" title="Rivers Cuomo">Rivers Cuomo</a> credited <i>Pet Sounds</i> as one of the band's biggest influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[263]</a></sup></p>
<p>Novelist <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Pynchon" title="Thomas Pynchon">Thomas Pynchon</a> was played <i>Pet Sounds</i> by journalist <a href="/wiki/Jules_Siegel" title="Jules Siegel">Jules Siegel</a> shortly after the album's release; at the time, Pynchon was unaware why the journalist had been interested in covering the group. After listening, Pynchon was reportedly in a "stunned pleasure", sighing softly before saying, "Ohhhhh, now I understand."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[264]</a></sup> The album motivated film producer <a href="/wiki/Bill_Pohlad" title="Bill Pohlad">Bill Pohlad</a> to direct the 2014 biopic on Brian WIlson, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Love_%26_Mercy" title="Love &amp; Mercy">Love &amp; Mercy</a></i>, which includes a substantial depiction of the album's making, with actor <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dano" title="Paul Dano">Paul Dano</a> playing Brian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[265]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tributes">Tributes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tributes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys_in_popular_culture" title="The Beach Boys in popular culture">The Beach Boys in popular culture</a></div>
<p><i>Pet Sounds</i> has inspired <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tribute_album" title="Tribute album">tribute albums</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Do_It_Again:_A_Tribute_to_Pet_Sounds" title="Do It Again: A Tribute to Pet Sounds">Do It Again: A Tribute to Pet Sounds</a></i> (2005), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Vitamin_String_Quartet" title="The Vitamin String Quartet">The String Quartet Tribute to the Beach Boys' Pet Sounds</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/MOJO_Presents_Pet_Sounds_Revisited" title="MOJO Presents Pet Sounds Revisited">MOJO Presents Pet Sounds Revisited</a></i> (2012), and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Tribute_to_Pet_Sounds" title="A Tribute to Pet Sounds">A Tribute to Pet Sounds</a></i> (2016).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[266]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Pet_Sounds_in_the_Key_of_Dee" title="Pet Sounds in the Key of Dee">Pet Sounds in the Key of Dee</a></i> (2007) is a mashup of the album with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J-Dilla" title="J-Dilla">J-Dilla</a>, by record producer Bullion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[267]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the mid-1990s, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schneider" title="Robert Schneider">Robert Schneider</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Apples_in_Stereo" title="The Apples in Stereo">The Apples in Stereo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_McIntyre_(musician)" title="Jim McIntyre (musician)">Jim McIntyre</a> of <a href="/wiki/Von_Hemmling" title="Von Hemmling">Von Hemmling</a> founded <a href="/wiki/Pet_Sounds_Studio" title="Pet Sounds Studio">Pet Sounds Studio</a>, which served as the venue for many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elephant_6" title="Elephant 6">Elephant 6</a> projects such as <a href="/wiki/Neutral_Milk_Hotel" title="Neutral Milk Hotel">Neutral Milk Hotel</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Aeroplane_Over_the_Sea" title="In the Aeroplane Over the Sea">In the Aeroplane Over the Sea</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Olivia_Tremor_Control" title="The Olivia Tremor Control">the Olivia Tremor Control</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Music_from_the_Unrealized_Film_Script:_Dusk_at_Cubist_Castle" title="Music from the Unrealized Film Script: Dusk at Cubist Castle">Dusk at Cubist Castle</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Foliage:_Animation_Music_Volume_One" title="Black Foliage: Animation Music Volume One">Black Foliage</a></i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Brian_Wilson_Presents_Pet_Sounds_Live" title="Brian Wilson Presents Pet Sounds Live">Brian Wilson Presents Pet Sounds Live</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pet_Sounds_50th_Anniversary_World_Tour" title="Pet Sounds 50th Anniversary World Tour">Pet Sounds 50th Anniversary World Tour</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brian_Wilson_20160328_185747_Byron_Bay_(26182663245).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2764" data-file-width="4914" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Brian_Wilson_20160328_185747_Byron_Bay_%2826182663245%29.jpg/220px-Brian_Wilson_20160328_185747_Byron_Bay_%2826182663245%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Brian_Wilson_20160328_185747_Byron_Bay_%2826182663245%29.jpg/330px-Brian_Wilson_20160328_185747_Byron_Bay_%2826182663245%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Brian_Wilson_20160328_185747_Byron_Bay_%2826182663245%29.jpg/440px-Brian_Wilson_20160328_185747_Byron_Bay_%2826182663245%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brian_Wilson_20160328_185747_Byron_Bay_(26182663245).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wilson performing <i>Pet Sounds</i> as a solo artist at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byron_Bay_Bluesfest" title="Byron Bay Bluesfest">Byron Bay Bluesfest</a>, 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After its release, several selections from <i>Pet Sounds</i> became staples for the group's live performances, including "Wouldn't It Be Nice", "Sloop John B" and "God Only Knows". Other songs were performed, albeit sporadically and infrequently through the years, and the album was never performed in its entirety with every original group member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Beach_Boys_Tour_Statistics_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Beach_Boys_Tour_Statistics-305">[268]</a></sup> In the late 1990s, Carl Wilson vetoed an offer for the Beach Boys to perform <i>Pet Sounds</i> in full for ten shows, reasoning that the studio arrangements were too complex for the stage, and that Brian could not possibly sing his original parts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarlin2006286_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarlin2006286-306">[269]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a solo artist, Brian performed the entire album live in 2000 with a different orchestra in each venue, and on three occasions without orchestra on his 2002 tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[270]</a></sup> Recordings from Wilson's 2002 concert tour were released as <i><a href="/wiki/Brian_Wilson_Presents_Pet_Sounds_Live" title="Brian Wilson Presents Pet Sounds Live">Brian Wilson Presents Pet Sounds Live</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2004378_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2004378-308">[271]</a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Dorian Lynskey says that the shows helped establish the now-ubiquitous practice of artists playing "classic albums" in their entirety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[272]</a></sup> In 2013, he performed the album at two shows, unannounced, also with Jardine as well as original Beach Boys guitarist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_Marks_(musician)" title="David Marks (musician)">David Marks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[273]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[274]</a></sup> In 2016, Wilson performed the album at several events in Australia, Japan, Europe, Canada and the United States. The tour was planned as his final performances of the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[275]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_history">Release history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Release history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Pet_Sounds_Sessions" title="The Pet Sounds Sessions">The Pet Sounds Sessions</a></div>
<p><i>Pet Sounds</i> has had many different reissues since its release in 1966, including remastered mono and stereo versions. Its first reissue was in 1972,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> when it was packaged as a bonus LP with the Beach Boys' latest album <i><a href="/wiki/Carl_and_the_Passions_%E2%80%93_%22So_Tough%22" title='Carl and the Passions – "So Tough"'>Carl and the Passions – "So Tough"</a></i>. The first release of the album on CD came in 1990, when it was released with the addition of three bonus tracks: "Unreleased Backgrounds",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[nb 38]</a></sup> "Hang On to Your Ego", and "Trombone Dixie" all of which were described as unreleased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAtimes2_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-LAtimes2-314">[276]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1997, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pet_Sounds_Sessions" title="The Pet Sounds Sessions">The Pet Sounds Sessions</a></i> box set was released. It included the original mono release of <i>Pet Sounds</i>, the very first stereo release (created by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Linett" title="Mark Linett">Mark Linett</a>), and three discs of unreleased material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAtimes_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-LAtimes-315">[277]</a></sup> In 2001, <i>Pet Sounds</i> was re-released with the mono and improved stereo versions, plus "Hang on to Your Ego" as a bonus track, all on one disc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAtimes_315-1"><a href="#cite_note-LAtimes-315">[277]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[278]</a></sup> On August 29, 2006, Capitol released a 40th Anniversary edition, containing a new 2006 remaster of the original mono mix, DVD mixes (stereo and Surround Sound), and a "making of" documentary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMIssions_248-1"><a href="#cite_note-EMIssions-248">[217]</a></sup> The discs were released in a regular jewel box and a deluxe edition was released in a green fuzzy box. A two disk colored gatefold vinyl set was released with green (stereo) and yellow (mono) disks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2016, a 50th anniversary edition box set presents the remastered album in both stereo and mono forms alongside studio sessions outtakes, alternate mixes, and live recordings. Of the 104 tracks, only 14 were previously unreleased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[279]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Track_listing">Track listing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Track listing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<th class="tlheader mbox-text" colspan="4" style="text-align:left;background-color:#fff">Side two</th>

Wilson">1994 court case</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoeTobler200922.2C_25_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoeTobler200922.2C_25-39">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pet_Sounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ambox_current_red.svg"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(June 2016)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The following credits are sourced from liner notes included with the 1999 mono/stereo reissue of <i>Pet Sounds</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PS1999_318-0"><a href="#cite_note-PS1999-318">[280]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Precise_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="2016 reissue corrects erroneous credits from the 1999 issue">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> except where otherwise noted.</p>
<p><b>The Beach Boys</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Al_Jardine" title="Al Jardine">Al Jardine</a> – lead, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harmony_vocals" title="Harmony vocals">harmony</a> and backing vocals, <a href="/wiki/Tambourine" title="Tambourine">tambourine</a> (uncertain)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bruce_Johnston" title="Bruce Johnston">Bruce Johnston</a> – harmony and backing vocals</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mike_Love" title="Mike Love">Mike Love</a> – lead, harmony and backing vocals</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brian_Wilson" title="Brian Wilson">Brian Wilson</a> – lead, harmony and backing vocals, <a href="/wiki/Organ_(music)" title="Organ (music)">organ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dog_whistles" title="Dog whistles">dog whistles</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETunbridge2010173_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETunbridge2010173-43">[36]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sound_effects" title="Sound effects">sound effects</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETunbridge2010173_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETunbridge2010173-43">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tracks_36-12"><a href="#cite_note-tracks-36">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carl_Wilson" title="Carl Wilson">Carl Wilson</a> – lead, harmony and backing vocals, <a href="/wiki/Guitar" title="Guitar">guitar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Twelve-string_guitar" title="Twelve-string guitar">twelve-string guitar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dennis_Wilson" title="Dennis Wilson">Dennis Wilson</a> – harmony and backing vocals, <a href="/wiki/Drum_kit" title="Drum kit">drums</a></li>
</ul>
<p><b>Production</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bruce_Botnick" title="Bruce Botnick">Bruce Botnick</a> – engineer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chuck_Britz" title="Chuck Britz">Chuck Britz</a> – engineer</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=H._Bowen_David&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="H. Bowen David (page does not exist)">H. Bowen David</a> – engineer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Larry_Levine" title="Larry Levine">Larry Levine</a> – engineer</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Guests</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tony_Asher" title="Tony Asher">Tony Asher</a> – plucked piano strings on "You Still Believe in Me"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tracks_36-13"><a href="#cite_note-tracks-36">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Terry_Melcher" title="Terry Melcher">Terry Melcher</a> – tambourine on "That's Not Me" (uncertain) and "Here Today"</li>
</ul>

<td>UK Top 40 Singles</td>
<td style="text-align:center;">2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1966</td>
<td>"Sloop John B"</td>
<td>UK Top 40 Singles</td>
<td style="text-align:center;">2</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
